 The day before, on 31 October 1984, former Prime Minister Indira Gandhi was shot dead by her own security forces

 1
 Indian Army - Salute the front with open toes We all must have seen army officers and soldiers saluting somewhere
 ve khule panjon se or daahine haath se sailyut karte hai
 All the fingers are open in front and the thumb is attached together
 yah apane se senior ormatahatke prati sammaan prakat karne kaa jariya he
 It also states that there is no weapon of any kind in the hand of the next
 2
 Indian Navy - Open palm that points towards the ground
 For the salute in the Indian Navy, the palm is held with the head part in such a way that there is a 90 degree angle between the palm and the ground
 is sailyut ke peeche ek badi vajah navy main karyratnavikon or sainikonke jahaaj par kaam karne kii vajah se gandi ho gai hatheliyon ko chhipaana he

 The process of altering, reforming or making a bill innocent in the legislative assembly is called 'amendment'
 sabha yaa samiti ke prastaav ke shodhan kii kriya ke liye bhi is shabd kaa prayog hota he
 No matter how carefully the constitution of any country should be made, but the limits of human imagination are bound
 1
 First Amendment (1951): Through this, an attempt was made to remove some of the practical difficulties in implementing the fundamental rights related to freedom, equality and property
 bhaashan evam abhivyakti ke mul adhikaron par isamen uchit pratibandh kii vyavastha kii gai
 Also, the ninth schedule was added to the Constitution by this amendment, in which the mentioned laws cannot be tested under the powers of judicial review of the Supreme Court
 2
 Second Amendment (1952): Under this the representation in Lok Sabha was rearranged on the basis of 1951 census
 3
 Third Amendment (1954): Under the Seventh Schedule, the 33rd entry of the concurrent list was replaced by food grains, fodder for animals, raw cotton, jute etc
, whose production and supply can be controlled by the government if it is understood in the public interest
 
 4
 Fourth Amendment (1955): In the event of personal property being taken over by the state in the public interest, the court cannot conduct an examination in respect of its compensation
 5
 Fifth Amendment (1955): This amendment was amended in Article 3, in which the President was empowered to state the central statutes proposed by the State Legislatures to affect the territories, boundaries, etc
 of their states
 One can set a time frame for sending ideas
 6
 Sixth Amendment (1956): By this amendment, the Union has been empowered to levy tax on certain items under the inter-state Sales Tax by changing the Union List of the Seventh Schedule
 7
 Santwa Amendment (1956): States were reorganized on linguistic basis by this amendment, dividing them into states and union territories, ending the classification of states into the next three categories
 saath hi, inke anuroop centre evam rajya kii vidhaan palikaon main siton ko punarvyavasthit kiya gaya
 8
 aathvaan sanshodhan (1959):iske antargat centre evam rajyon ke nimna sadanon main anusuchit jaati, anusuchit janajati evam angl bhartiya samudaayon ke aarakshan sambandhi praavdhaanon ko das varshon arthath 1970 tak badha diya gaya
 9
 nauveen sanshodhan (1960):iske dwaara samvidhan kii pratham anusuchee main parivartan karke bharat or pakistan ke bich 1958 kii sandhi kii sharton ke anusaar berubaari, khulanaa aadi kshetra pakistan ko de die gaye
 10
 dasvaan sanshodhan (1961):iske antargat bhootpurv portugali antah kshetron dadar evam nagar haveli ko bharat main shaamil kar unhen centre shasit pradesh kaa darja de diya gaya
 11
 11waan sanshodhan (1962):iske antargat uparashtrapati ke nirvachan ke praavdhaanon main parivartan kar, is sandarbh main donon sadanon ke sanyukt adhiveshan ko bulaayaa gaya
 It is also determined that the election of President or Vice President cannot be challenged on the basis of vacancy of the post in the electoral college
 12
 12th Amendment (1962): Under this, Goa, Daman and Diu were included as Union Territories in India by amending the First Schedule of the Constitution
 13
 13th Amendment (1962): Under this, special provisions regarding Nagaland were adopted and given the status of a state
 14
 14th Amendment (1963): It incorporated Puducherry into India as a union territory
 saath hi iske dwaara himachal pradesh, manipur, tripura, goa, daman or div tathaa puducheri centre shasit pradeshon main vidhaan palika evam mantriparishad kii sthapana kii gai
 15
 15waan sanshodhan (1963):iske antargat ucch nyaayalay ke nyaayadhishon kii sevamukthi kii aayu 60 se badhaakar 62 varsh kar di gai tathaa avkaash praapt nyaayadhishon kii ucch nyaayalay main niyukti se sabandhit praavdhaan banaae gaye
 16
 16waan sanshodhan (1963):iske dwaara desh kii samprabhutaa evam akhandta ke hit main mul adhikaron par kuch pratibandh lagane ke praavdhaan rakhe gaye saath hi teesri anusuchee main bhi parivartan kar shapath grahan ke antargat 'main bharat kii swatantraaa evam akhandta ko banaae rakhuunga' joda gaya
 17
 17waan sanshodhan (1964):isamen sampatti ke adhikaron main or bhi sanshodhan karte hue kuch anya bhoomi sudhaar praavdhaanon ko nauveen anusuchee main rakhaa gaya, jinaki vaidhata pariksha sarvocch nyaayalay dwaara nahin kii ja sakati thi
 18
 18waan sanshodhan (1966):iske antargat punjab kaa bhashiya aadhaar par punargathan karte hue punjabi bhashi kshetra ko punjab evam hindi bhashi kshetra ko haryana ke rup main gathit kiya gaya
 The hilly regions were given to Himachal Pradesh and Chandigarh was made a union territory
 19
 19th Amendment (1966): Under this, the rights of the Election Commission were changed and the High Courts were empowered to hear election petitions
 20
 20th Amendment (1966): Under this, the appointment of some district judges appointed on the basis of irregularity was given validity
 21
 21st Amendment (1967): It incorporated the Sindhi language as the fifteenth language under the Eighth Schedule of the Constitution
 22
 22nd Amendment (1969): a new state of Meghalaya was carved out of Assam by it
 23
 23rd Amendment (1969): Under this, the reservation of Scheduled Castes and Scheduled Tribes in the Legislatures and nomination of people of anglo-indian community was extended for ten years
 24
 24th Amendment (1971): Under this amendment, the power of the Parliament was clarified that it can amend any part of the amendment, including the fundamental rights under Part Three, as also determined
 That when the amendment bill is passed by both the houses before the President, it will be binding on the President to give the property
 25
 26th Amendment (1971): Under this, special titles of rulers of the erstwhile indigenous states and their privy purses were abolished
 26
 27th Amendment (1971): Under this, Mizoram and Arunachal Pradesh were established in the union territories
 27
 29th Amendment (1972): Under this the Kerala Land Reforms (amendment) Act, 1969 and Kerala Land Reforms (amendment) Act, 1971 were placed in the Ninth Schedule of the Constitution, so that its constitutional validity is not challenged in the court
 Could
 28
 31st Amendment (1973): Through this the number of members of the Lok Sabha was reduced from 525 to 545 and the representation of Union Territories was reduced from 25 to 20
 29
 32nd Amendment (1974): Resignation is invalidated under pressure or coercion by members of Parliament and Legislatures and the Speaker has the right to accept only voluntarily and proper resignation
 29
 34th Amendment (1974): Under this, twenty Land Reforms Acts passed by various states were given entry in the Ninth Schedule and they were exempted from the test of constitutional validity by the court
 30
 35th Amendment (1974): Under this, the status of the protected states of Sikkim was abolished and entered into India as an allied state
 31
 36th Amendment (1975): Under this, Sikkim was made the twenty-second state of India
 32
 37th Amendment (1975): Under this, declaration of a state of emergency and the issuance of ordinance by the President, Rajyapala and the administrative heads of Union Territories were disputed, freeing them from judicial reconsideration
 33
 39th Amendment (1975): By this the disputes related to the election of President, Vice President, Prime Minister and Speaker of Lok Sabha were exempted from judicial trial
 34
 41st Amendment (1976): By this the age limit for the service of the members of the State Public Service Commission was reduced to 60 years, but the maximum age of retirement of the members of the Union Public Service Commission was 65 years
 35
 42nd Amendment (1976): It brought about major changes in the constitution, the main of which were the following
 (k)samvidhan kii prastaavna main 'samaajawaadee' 'dharmanirpeksh' evam 'ekta or akhandta' aadi shabd jode gaye
 (B) All policy directive principles were ensured supremacy over fundamental rights
 (ga)iske antargat samvidhan main das moulik kartavyon ko anuchhed 51(k), (bhaag-iv k) ke antargat joda gaya
 (D) It constituted the constitution mainly by judicial trial
 (ng)sabhi vidhaan sabhaaon evam lok sabha kii siton kii sankhya ko is shatabdi ke ant tak ke sthir kar diya gaya
 (F) The duration of the Lok Sabha and the Vidhan Sabhas has been reduced from five to six years, (g) It has been determined that on the validity of any central law, the Supreme Court and the High Court will examine the validity of the state law
 saath hi, yah bhi nirdhaarit kiya gaya ki kisi sanvaidhanik vaidhata ke prashn par paanch se adhik nyayadhishon kii bench dwaara di tihaai bahumat se nirnay diya janaa chahie or yadi nyaayadhishon kii sankhya paanch tak ho to nirnay sarvasammati se hona chahie
 (H) By this, the subjects of forest wealth, education, population-control etc
 were reduced from the state list to the concurrent list
 (jha)iske antargat nirdhaarit kiya gaya ki raashtrapati mantriparishad evam uske pramukh pradhanmantri kii salaah ke anusaar kaary karegaa
 (K) It gave Parliament the authority to enact laws to deal with anti-national activities and established supremacy
 36
 44th Amendment (1978): In order to impose national emergency, internal rebellion was replaced by military revolt and other provisions related to emergency were changed so that they are not misused
 iske dwaara sampatti ke adhikaar ko moulik adhikaron ke bhaag se hataa kar vidheyak (kanoonee) adhikaron kii shrenee main rakh diya gaya
 The term of Lok Sabha and State Legislative Assemblies was reduced from 6 years to 5 years again
 ucchtam nyaayalay ko raashtrapati tathaa uparashtrapati ke nirvachan sambandhi vivaad ko hal karne kii adhikarita pradaan kii gai

 50waan sanshodhan (1984):iske dwaara anuchhed 33 main sanshodhan kar sainya sevaaon kii poorak sevaaon main kaary karne waalon ke liye aavashyak suchanaaen ekatrit karne, desh kii sampatti kii raksha karne or kanoon tathaa vyavastha se sambandhit daayitv bhi die gaye

 39
 53rd Amendment (1986): Under this, Mizoram was given state status by adding clause 'G' in Article 371
 40

 61st Amendment (1989): It proposed to reduce the age limit for voting from 21 years to 18 lanes
 47

 48
 69th Amendment (1991): Delhi was made a National Capital Territory and the Legislative Assembly and Council of Ministers were provided for the Union Territory of Delhi
 49
 70th Amendment (1992): Members of the Legislative Assemblies of the Union Territories of Delhi and Puducherry were included in the electoral college for the President
 50
 71st Amendment (1992): Konkani, Manipuri and Nepali languages were included in the Eighth Schedule
 51
 73rd Amendment (1992-93): Under this, the eleventh schedule was added to the constitution
 iske panchayat raaj sambandhi praavdhaanon ko sammilit kiya gaya he
